What interns did:
CUTAC targets RNA Pol II Ser5p with a low-salt tagmentation step so that antibody- tethered Tn5 cuts at accessible regulatory DNA, producing high-res, low-background maps of open chromatin regions even from very few... I study the phenomenon of suspended animation in the nematode C. When deprived of oxygen, adult nematodes can survive in an alternative death-like state for anywhere from 48 to 72 hours at room temperature. This phenomenon, termed suspended animation, can be replicated in other animals - including...

Notable activities / experiences:
Using the Hutch cluster and working in the Steam Plant. The Roth lab is unique in how it conducts science. Rather than searching for genotype- phenotype correlations, my mentor finds it more convenient to assay for life and death directly. • Created artificial TCRs including developing an online outline • Learned college level immunology concepts • Invited to retreats where new research was presented • Hands-on lab...

External research note:
Major Seattle cancer research and care center. Its official site describes 50 years of research and care, global research reach, 6000+ employees, and three Nobel Prize winners associated with Fred Hutch researchers. (https://www.fredhutch.org/en/about.html)

## UW Elementary Particle Experiment Group

Fit score: 100/100

Contacts:
- Shih-Chieh Hsu — schsu@uw.edu
- Professor Shih-Chieh Hsu — schsu@uw.edu

What interns did:
The internship consists of two stages, the first of which is going over basic ML (Neural Networks, CNN, Transformers, etc) through labs. The second stage involves choosing a research direction to work on, where students will get assigned a mentor. Spend the first semester completing the PHYS 417 UW course, learning Machine Learning structures and code. The course specifically explores the applications of ML in the real world physical environment. Every week is spent on a different lab, then weekly the students...

Notable activities / experiences:
• Experiencing a research symposium and presenting your work at the end of the Internship • Receiving guidance and help from Post- Doc Researchers • Conducted an independent research project under mentorship from university researchers and instructors. • Learned how research is performed at the college level, from forming a research question to presenting final results. I got to work with EveNet, which is this...

External research note:
Professor Shih-Chieh Hsu is a UW Physics professor in nuclear and particle experiment whose biography includes ATLAS/LHC work, electroweak leadership, and physics-plus-machine-learning courses. (https://phys.washington.edu/people/shih-chieh-hsu)

## Seattle Children's Research Institute

Fit score: 100/100
Best for: Research, Biomedical / Health, CS / AI / Data
Categories in catalogs: Bio/Medical Research, Research, Research: Bio/Medical
Location: Seattle (307 Westlake Ave and 1916 Boren Ave), Seattle, online/in person at Jack MacDonald Building, Seattle Internship description attle Children's houses a wide variety of labs ranging from molecular biology to tech research. I work in the attle Children's Innovative Technologies Lab, which researches ways to apply tech in autism research. As an intern, I cleaned and entered data from past studies, wrote literature reviews and compiled publications with my mentor, and worked on side projects relevant to behavioral and tech research. Seattle Children's typically only hires UW students, so as a high schooler I never had access to the system or PHI but was still able to help in other ways. Unique experiences Writing a literature review on applications of eye tracking in autism research Helping to research and compile sources for a book on eye tracking as a potential psychiatric biomarker Working on Al generated images for an equity in healthcare careers comic book surprised you most? I was surprised by the amount of coordination and time that goes into a successful study, we were still processing data from studies completed 8 years ago and working to publish any findings. t is your greatest takeaway(s) from the internship experience?, Seattle (307 Westlake AVE) Internship description At the Vaughan Lab in the Seattle Children's Research Institute, Center for Global Infectious Disease, the primary focus is research into malaria through the use genetic recombination with the ultimate goa of alleviating the suffering of those infected. My role was largely that of a research assistant, helping the research scientists with their experiments, recording data, and creating data tables to be published. My work primarily dealt with the P. falciparum strand, genetic crosses of the lab-strain with wild-strains from across Africa (Sudan, Mali, and Malawi), end developing a vaccine that is more representative of malaria in the field. By measuring and comparing the effectiveness of these hybrid crosses at infecting the liver, we sought to determine which hybrid is most suitable and effective for vaccine development. Unique experiences Hear from scientists that speak at global conferences. Work with human malaria and humanized mouse livers through laboratory procedures such as PCR, IFA, microscopy etc. Analyze different research papers and learn more about publication through first-hand experience.
Catalog years: 2026, 2025, 2024, 2023
Signals: repeat placement, recent, direct email, web-checked, OCR recovered
Contacts:
- Jonathan Tang — Jonathan.Tang@seattlechildrens.org
- Ashley Vaughan — ashley.vaughan@seattlechildrens.org
- Ashley Vaughan — Ashley-Vauqhan@seattlechildrens.org

What interns did:
The Tang Lab focuses on research into the brain and determining where the conscious is located in the brain. My role as an intern was to aid with quantifying mouse movement with deep learning models such as DeepLabCut. The Vaughan lab is part of the Center for Global Infectious Disease at Seattle Children's Research Institute. This internship is centered around doing research on your own on a chosen topic of atmospheric physics. I was introduced to the basics and given the fundamental tools needed to run a forecast. ## Emit Lab

Fit score: 50/100
Best for: Biomedical / Health, Engineering / Physics, CS / AI / Data
Categories in catalogs: Computer Science & Engineering
Location: UW Seattle Internship description Medical imaging in its current form is expensive, inefficient, and inaccessible. We have worked on a methodology to stitch images from the OpenMV H7 camera such that in-depth LSCI imaging can be overlaid with the area of the body being captured. This will enable more efficient imaging of subcutaneous venous structures and injuries, providing a hand-held, quick alternative to traditional medical imaging. We focus on the panoramic stitching of the images captured by our handheld camera, or putting segments of separately captured images together to accurately capture a larger area. Namely, we've focused on the preservation of sufficient detail and accuracy in the final image so that it may be useful for medical applications. Unique experiences Working through unknown code and writing documentation Learning about ML applications in image processing Creating and tinkering with algorithms and workflows for tangible outcomes

## Kaeberlein Lab, University of Washington Dpt. Of Pathology

Fit score: 50/100
Best for: Research, CS / AI / Data, Biomedical / Health
Categories in catalogs: Research
Location: Seattle
Catalog years: 2021
Signals: direct email, academic mentor
Contacts:
- Ben Blue — benblue@uw.edu

What interns did:
Primary research goal of screening natural/synthetic compounds in C. elegans to identify drugs that have the potential to delay the onset of/alleviate symptoms associated with neurodegenerative diseases such as Parkinson's and Alzheimer's diseases. Interns do data annotation on images of c. elegans for developing a neural network that will allow the ability to investigate aging and aging interventions. Working on neural network to identify age of onset of Alzheimer's disease through analysis face images.

Notable activities / experiences:

• Designed covers for each episode that were published on Spotify/Apple Podcasts • Created animations for episodes to be published on social media • Produced merchandise through screen printing/machine embroidery –... • Created other social media posts – videos/graphics • Sat through podcast recordings with leading surgeons
